Navy Standards Primary Laboratory has an anechoic chamber. Probably not the quietest but likely within the top five. I spent two minutes inside of it and it was maddening.  1. we don't realize how attuned we are to room reflections until they are no longer there,  2. The sound of one's heartbeat and breathing becomes the loudest sound and it's really unsettling. 0/10 recommend.
Dude I can hang out in there for days. Love it. I actually watched this video 3 years ago and then built my entire room that I sleep in with similar materials to this. My room is not -9 decibels. Its around 4-6 decibals. I ended up having to not only get a more expensive higher quality TV that made less sound but I also had to get rid of my ceiling fans and put in specialty lights because my room is so quiet that it makes those things sound incredibly loud and become a great annoyance. I ended up putting in a secondary small AC unit to power my room and I built the AC ducts with conical materials That you would end up using in like a sound room so that it wouldn't make a lot of noise coming into the room and ended up being great. I grew up having severe insomnia and have had to be on a myriad of cocktails to shut down my mind put me to sleep. Now I'm only down to one of them, I used to take three. Not only that but the only one that I'm left on was the less potent of all three. It was definitely a project and a pain in the ass but absolutely worth it. Changed my life.
As someone with tinnitus, I suspect that this room would be profoundly unpleasant.

Fascinating -- fun vid, thanks!  Not a math genius, here, but I'm actually really interested in the design of this room's surfaces: I like the massive scale of the ridges (word?) -- that's got to be great for low-frequency, high energy sound waves, and also the addition of the netting over the face of each rib to create surface turbulences (reducing energy and creating destructive reflections, I'm guessing) across the surfaces, but I've so many questions and ideas, now: I'm wondering whether it would work better to tilt or curve the netting's splines as you would tilt the ribs of a helical slake, and maybe the geometry of the peaks of each ridge should be razor-sharp (ish)? I'll bet the size, shape and angle of each peak could change as the array approaches the corners of the room, and perhaps the ends of each ridge could be shaped to interact even more quietly with the faces of the adjacent ridges (and should those even be flat?);  Perhaps an open mesh floor could be used to remove all those reflections, as well: in other words, just how deep can this quiet room "rabbit hole" go? 6:47 NOT TRUE.  The stomach empties out to your RIGHT into the duodenum (unless you were born with situs inversus or some similar anatomic anomaly).  Laying on your right side, Mr. Gravity is your friend and will automatically cause stuff in your stomach to drain out into the duodenum even if your stomach is not contracting that much.  If you lay on your left, food will sit in the fundus of the stomach and go nowhere until the stomach contracts and forces it out (against the pull of Mr. Gravity). Also, your esophagus enters your stomach on the LEFT side of the stomach.   So, laying on your left side, Mr. Gravity will pull that food and liquid sitting in the fundus of the stomach back OUT up into your esophagus. So laying on your left side is a great way to increase esophageal reflux (a.k.a., hearburn) and decrease gastric emptying.  I generally lay on my right side when lying down or sleeping.

Can you hear your heartbeat?
I once went to a cave with my school. We were guided up to a certain point that they called "the heart of the cave" or something of the sort, because it was supposedly very deep, and it was a big spatious hall. Then they had us all sit down wherever we wanted, turn of all lights, notifications and such, and be quiet and close our eyes for two minutes. It's been three or four years and I have never felt anything like it to this day: complete silence, complete darkness, even though you know there are several people in this place with you, it still feels like it's just you, alone, with your heartbeat and your bloodflow.  At some point I held halds with my friend (who I had a bit of a crush for) and I could also feel her warmth and her vibrations. That is a moment I will always cherish.

Two of my friends and me all guys in our high school days tried a version of this in my basement. We closed all the curtains, turned off the lights and played a game of tag or tackle in the darkness. You learned very quickly that sound was the enemy. You removed any jewelry, watches, and belts. Then you removed sneakers that could squeak on the tile floor. You could hear your ears, then your breathing, then your heartbeat. All knowing that you could be tackled or tackle at any time. It was like psychological torture. I called for an end and we turned on the lights. We NEVER played that game again.

ğŸ¤” I have to dispute the 150dB claim of â€œfront rowâ€ of a rock concert. Being in the music world for a while now Iâ€™d surmise that 150dB is at total peak transient - and thatâ€™s a maybe - why? Most active (powered) speakers have a total output handling of 130-137dB (at peak transient) before failure or driver distortion. That being said, most Rock concerts, if EQâ€™d correctly, achieve 110/115dB RMS with the peak transients around 118/122dB. RMS = Root Mean Squared. In other words, rms is the overall decibel (A-weighted) average throughout the program. 150dB is more like a Glock or a 12-gauge shotgun fired at 1 meter. These readings could be achieved from a high pressure microphone that possesses an unusually stiff capsule - and even then you may damage the mic. If you measure a rock concert, C-weighted or Z-weighted, maybe youâ€™d see some 130dB or 135dB.    Iâ€™m not trying to be difficult or a d*ck or a know-it-all, but after a particular level, one canâ€™t hear the music anymore because it overexcites the room modes within the venue and the sound engineer just turns the band back down after a few songs anyway. Sometimes this happens by as much as 12dB.   Most guitar amps wonâ€™t produce more than 120dB. 150dB is very difficult to achieve with EQâ€™d sound waves. As soon as you EQ anything youâ€™re messing with phase and the physical property of the wave form changes.

Cool and epic
For the last 25 years, people have had to endure "music"  (otherwise known as distracting noise) while trying to listen to instructional videos, documentaries, actors' dialogue in movies, and on and on. LOL
I've been in an acoustic room like that while in training for my acoustic technician certification long time ago.  You stand on a net, and under it there is more sound absorbing foam. So, no echo comes from the floor, and your brain registers that there is no floor. The sensation is like being on top of a building with no wind. I wasn't in the dark, but I felt my body very loud indeed. The most annoying thing is the incredible loud buzz in your ear. The engineer working there told me that this buzz would go away if I kept going regularly to the room. The worst part is that I never really stopped hearing that buzz. Since that date, it comes back sometimes when I am in a quiet place.

WOW COOL AND DRAMATIC OMG
When I lived in the dessert we had a generator on all day because we didn't live in a house we lived in a trailer, and when it was time for bed and we turned off the generator, it was silence. Pure silence. It was so quiet that it was loud, I could hear my heart beat as if someone banged two pots together, I could also hear my blood flow to my head and I would always hear this...hum. It wasn't quite either, it was almost like my lullaby. There were different types of hums here and there though. Sometimes it would be really loud, really high-pitch, really low-pitch, sometimes it was so low that it made me want to scream. Just to be able to hear a different sound. The sounds gave me nightmares. I once had a nightmare where my mom died at a gas station because she left her car on while putting gas in it. I was 7 and I didn't know that could happen, but I dreamt of it. The thing that freaked me out the most is that I knew it was my mom....my mom went to jail when I was barely four. I don't even remember what she looks like. But then we moved from California to Missouri(wish we didn't)and we don't use a generator anymore. We have normal electricity so now its no longer loud at day. It's not really quite at night, there's a lot of wind so I don't hear the hums anymore..I almost miss them...

In a small little town there lived a hero who was considered to be the most powerful and wise person by everyone in that town. But one fine day the hero is challenged by a worthy opponent from another town (the pork chop). After a fight the hero is defeated and the pork chop takes his place as the the most powerful and wise person of that town. The hero then embarks on a journey to learn more and find a solution to finally defeat the pork chop. He finds a sensei who agrees to give him the key to defeating the pork chop only if he is successful in beating a world record (sitting in the room).The hero goes into the room and about 10 minutes later the hero feels like giving up. But he then experiences a flashback of how the pork chop ridicules him and tells him that he is good at nothing. Wanting to prove the pork chop wrong  the hero is determined to continue the challenge. Soon the hero is victorious and finds out that the sensei actually tricked him into thinking that there was a world record for him to beat. Sensei told him this was the only way to teach the hero how to defeat the pork chop. He goes back to his town where he finds the pork chop waiting for him on the throne at 2 am. In a final epic battle the hero uses the experience and power he gained from the quiet room to completely wipe the pork chop from existence. The hero finally defeats the pork chop and claims victory.
